## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a non-linear harmonic oscillator, involving position x, velocity v, and time t. The governing equation is a second-order ODE where dv/dt depends on restoring force (function of x), damping (function of v), and possibly external driving (function of t), characteristic of mechanical oscillator systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, no damping or forcing)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear viscous damping)
- Forced damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal external driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening cubic nonlinearity with damping)
- Duffing oscillator with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (self-sustained limit cycle oscillations)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - v**2) * v (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping leading to limit cycle)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * abs(v) (drag proportional to velocity squared)
- Dry friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (Coulomb friction, constant magnitude opposing motion)
- Asymmetric restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity breaking symmetry)
- Power-law stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x * abs(x)**(c1 - 1) (generalized nonlinear restoring force with tunable exponent)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness modulation)
- Bistable system: dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (double-well potential, e.g., Duffing with negative linear term)
- Exponential restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * (exp(c1 * x) - 1) (Toda oscillator type nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force is an odd function of displacement: dv_dt contains term -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 or similar odd powers for symmetric potentials
- Damping is proportional to velocity: dv_dt contains term -c * v for linear viscous dissipation
- Limit cycle behavior: dv_dt has multiplicative coupling between x and v, e.g., (1 - x**2) * v (Van der Pol) or (1 - v**2) * v (Rayleigh)
- External periodic driving: dv_dt includes explicit time-dependent term, usually trigonometric function like sin(c * t) or cos(c * t)
- Dry friction/Coulomb damping: dv_dt includes sign(v) or tanh(c*v) to model constant magnitude friction independent of speed
- Symmetry breaking: presence of even-order terms in x (e.g., x**2) indicates asymmetric potential and directional bias in restoring force
- Bistable / double-well potential: negative linear stiffness term (c0 * x with c0 > 0) combined with positive cubic term -c1 * x**3 produces two stable equilibria
- Parametric resonance: stiffness modulated by a periodic function of time, as in (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * x, can lead to exponential growth of oscillations
- Hardening vs softening spring: cubic term sign determines whether stiffness increases (negative -c1 * x**3) or decreases (positive +c1 * x**3) with displacement magnitude
- Generalized nonlinearity: odd power-law terms like -x * abs(x)**(n-1) produce a family of oscillators with tunable anharmonicity
